				<h3 class="notes">Notas:</h3>
				<ul class="notes">
					<li id="item_HR5NURL6">
<div><div>
<h1>Mitchell and Latour: Two approaches to networks</h1>
</div>
<div>
<blockquote>
<p>Kapferer, B. (2014, octubre 29). Mitchell and Latour: Two approaches to networks. Leading Manchester sociologists (1964-2014), University of Manchester.&nbsp;<a rel="noopener" href="https://youtu.be/PyCnqF_wPOA" target="_blank">https://youtu.be/PyCnqF_wPOA</a></p>
</blockquote>
</div>
<div><hr></div>
<div>
<p>Para resumir: Los enfoques entre Latour y Mitchell son muy distintos. Kapferer meciona que Mitchell se hubiera referido a las propuestas de Latour como meras metáforas e inculso acientíficas. Por otro lado Latour diría que el enfoque de Mitchell acentúa el sociocentrismo de los análisis al que él se opone. Kapferer menciona que las la dirección matemática de Mitchell iba más allá del sociocentrismo.</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>Mientras que Latour utiliza el concepto de red como una metáfora para estudiar etnográficamente la construcción de la ciencia, para Mitchell es una herramienta que puede usarse para estudiar científicamente los fenómenos antropológicos.</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>Estes es el resumen de&nbsp;<a rel="noopener" href="https://egalitarianism.no/michell-latour-two-approaches-networks-elementary-critical-considerations/" target="_blank">Kapferer</a>:</p>
</div>
<div>
<blockquote>
<p>The lecture begins with a discussion of Clyde Mitchell’s network perspective, its grounding in anthropological ethnography and its connection to the situational analytic perspective of Gluckman’s “Manchester School”. Gluckman was concerned to make Malinowski’s anthropological ethnographic innovation, developed in small-scale isolated traditional societies, relevant to the analysis of social and political processes in the dynamic complex social worlds of modernity. His point is also larger: that is all social contexts no matter how isolated are enmeshed in larger global processes. Gluckman was, in this sense critical of what might be termed ‘island anthropology’ which related societies as enclosed isolated wholes. Mitchell’s approach to networks is influenced by Gluckman’s situational approach as well as his critique of that anthropology that treated of societies as isolated wholes. This had the seeds of a critique of the grand narrative approaches of modern sociological theory and their often retreat into abstraction and a losing of sight of the on the ground processes that such abstraction was given to comprehend as well as inattention to the larger fields of political and social process in which they are enmeshed. Mitchell’s network perspective extended along these lines moreover insisting that institutional analysis, for example, should be traced into detailed accounts of social processes that the network perspective was oriented towards. The lecture explores this direction and considers the importance of ideology and value in the dynamics of social networks. At this point the lecture demonstrates the similarities and differences between Mitchell and Latour’s approaches. One similarity is the movement away from the idea of society as an integrated totality. The major dissimilarity concerns the importance of value. This is stressed in Mitchell – a concern of his being the way new value is generated. Latour it will be argued stressed interconnections but without a concern for value. Furthermore in Latour the idea of network is very little other than an abstract metaphor. Mitchell is more concerned with converting a metaphor into a substantial methodological practice. The lecture more generally, and through its comparison of the Mitchell and Latour perspectives, develops towards a contemplation on the nature of a scientific understanding of the social which is the major direction and importance of Latour’s approach.</p>
</blockquote>
</div>
<div>
<p>El texto de John Scott tiene un buen resumen de los desarrollos de las redes sociales en antropología y sociología, para entrar con más profundidad.</p>
</div>
<div>
<h1>Pioneros del análisis de redes en antropología</h1>
</div>
<div>
<p>La teoría y metodología de redes sociales se desarrollo mayormente por un pequeño de antropólogos británicos asociados a la Universadad de Manchester. Principalmente podemos mencionar a John Barnes, Clyde Mitchell y Elizabeth Bott, quienes fueron parte de la Escuela de Manchester con influencias de Radcliffe-Brown y principalmente representados por la figura central de Max Gluckman. Este grupo de antropólogos enfatizaron el conflicto y el cambio en lugar de la cohesión e integración.</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>Mitchell se influencio en el análisis situacional de Gluckman que criticaba la tradición durkhemiana. Gluckman tenía influencias de los estudios de Evans-Pritchard.</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>La principal preocupación de Mitchell era desarrollar el concepto como una herramienta de análisis, no sólo una metáfora o un aparato metodológico. El concepto de red permitía hacer observaciones directas en campo de los individuos y al mismo tiempo hacer abstracciones a partir de él. Esto no era un abandono de lo social o lo cultural. A trvpes de él se podían entender y descubir procesos supraindividuales que podían ser ignorados.</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>El concepto crusaba varias categorías analíticas, clase, etnicidad, las decentralizaba y les quitaba sus obstacúlos.</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>Fueron criticados en tiempos de Mitchell. La idea de red volvío en un tiempo de un mundo conectado y con el desarrollo de redes digitales de comunicación. En ese periodo mucho a cambiado. Se reducen algunas consideraciones estructurales, institucionales, culturales, ideológicos y fuerzas de los procesos de las redes. Algunos proponentes del concepto esquivan estas consideraciones.</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>Clyde Mitchell no creía en la división entre sociología y antrop.</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>Mitchell adelantaba algunas consideraciones de Latour.</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>Los conceptos y herramientas de redes surgen del estudio de los cambios urbanos en África. Metodológicamente, surge como una herramienta para estudiar la complejidad de la urbanidad.</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>Análisis situacional --&gt; Análisis de redes / eran redes egocéntricas que analizaban grupos pequeños, en su tiempo no tuvo éxito en extenderse a otros ámbitos</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>Relaciones, su estructura, composición y calidad</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>Una de las mayores innovaciones estuvo a cargo de Elizabeth Bott, una antropóloga con intereses en psicoanálisis que se concentró en la dinámica de las relaciones.</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>John Barnes toma el concepto para estudiar Noruega.</p>
</div>
<div>
<ul>
<li>El concepto de redes era dinámica. Se pueden reestructurar.</li>
<li>Los componentes no deben considerarse valores independientes. Los componentes adquieren su valor de los demás componentes.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div>
<p>Para Mitchell la antropología estaba comprometida con la ciencia. La idea de RS podía ser una sintesis entre la observación, que por sí misma era completamente científica, y la integración con enfoques matemáticos. El trabajo de campo puede ser integrado con las técnicas matemáticas y estadísticas, cada una expandiendo sus potencialidades. La noción de RS podía integrar dos enfoques científicos como complementarios: observacional y experiencial por un lado, y otro abstracto y formal.</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>Extender las posibilidades de la observación y la experiencia etnográfica.</p>
</div>
<div>
<h2>Latour y Law</h2>
</div>
<div>
<p>Su enfoque es Anti-sociocéntrico. Posestructuralista o poshumanista.<br>La TAR enfatiza la agencia y dinámicas de actores no-humanos.</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>La genealogía de Latour desplaza la herencia socioantropológica a Durkheim y Mauss y recupera a mejor a Gabriel Tarde y Deleuze. Elementos heterogéneos, ensamble y reensamble, multiplicidad, rizomas, decentralización.</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>Menciona a Manuel Delanda como alguien con un enfoque similar al de Latour</p>
</div></div>
					</li>
				</ul>

			<li id="item_VEWFX3GW" class="item journalArticle">
			<h2>Network Analysis, Culture, and the Problem of Agency</h2>
				<table>
					<tr>
						<th>Tipo</th>
						<td>Artículo de revista académica</td>
					</tr>
					<tr>
						<th class="author">Autor</th>
						<td>Mustafa Emirbayer</td>
					</tr>
					<tr>
						<th class="author">Autor</th>
						<td>Jeff Goodwin</td>
					</tr>
					<tr>
					<th>Resumen</th>
						<td>Network analysis is one of the most promising currents in sociological research, and yet it has never been subjected to a theoretically informed assessment and critique. This article outlines the theoretical presuppositions of network analysis. It also distinguishes between three different (implicit) models in the network literature of the interrelations of social structure, culture, and human agency. It concludes that only a strategy for historical explanation that synthesizes social structural and cultural analysis can adequately explain the formation, reproduction, and transformation of networks themselves. The article sketches the broad contours of such a theoretical synthesis in the conclusion.</td>
					</tr>
					<tr>
					<th>Fecha</th>
						<td>1994</td>
					</tr>
					<tr>
					<th>Catálogo de biblioteca</th>
						<td>JSTOR</td>
					</tr>
					<tr>
					<th>URL</th>
						<td><a href="https://www.jstor.org/stable/2782580">https://www.jstor.org/stable/2782580</a></td>
					</tr>
					<tr>
					<th>Accedido</th>
						<td>28/12/2020 16:07:07</td>
					</tr>
					<tr>
					<th>Adicional</th>
						<td>Publisher: University of Chicago Press</td>
					</tr>
					<tr>
					<th>Volumen</th>
						<td>99</td>
					</tr>
					<tr>
					<th>Páginas</th>
						<td>1411-1454</td>
					</tr>
					<tr>
					<th>Publicación</th>
						<td>American Journal of Sociology</td>
					</tr>

						<td>6</td>

				<h3 class="notes">Notas:</h3>
				<ul class="notes">
					<li id="item_6F2Z7BWF">
<div><div>
<p>Esta lista tiene errores de origen, mejor ver el artículo original en el apéndice al final (<a rel="noopener" href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/L5FUWHQM?page=38" target="_blank">Emirbayer and Goodwin 1994:1448</a>) y es el anexo que contiene un glosario básico. <strong>Se complementa muy bien con los de Scott y el de Knoke.</strong></p>
</div>
<div><hr></div>
<div>
<p>The following definitions are meant to orient the general reader to the basic terms of network analysis as well as to convey the way in which certain more general sociological concepts have been "translated" into these terms.</p>
</div>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Actor: A person, group, organization, thing, event, and so on, linked to others in This is to as a "node".</li>
<li>Asymmetric tie: A relation whose form, content, or both s different for the inked actors. See also symmetric tie.</li>
<li>Block: A set of structurally equivalent actors in a multiplex network. See also multiplex network and&nbsp;structural equivalence.</li>
<li>Blockmodeling: A technique for finding or "partitioning" (and graphically representing) structurally equivalent actors or blocks) in a network.</li>
<li>Boundary problem: The problem of defining the population of actors to be studied through network analysis in a way which does not depend on a priori categories; in other words, the problem of delimiting the study of social networks which n reality may have no limits.</li>
<li>Catnet&nbsp;(from category and network): A socially cohesive set of structurally equivalent actors hypothesized as more able and likely to share ideas or a common culture and to engage n collective action than other sorts of real or latent groups. See also social cohesion.</li>
<li>Centrality: The number of an actor's ties to others, weighted by the number of the latter's ties to others.</li>
<li>Clique: A group of actors in which each is directly and strongly linked to all of the others. Compare social circle.</li>
<li>Content: The specific nature or type of relation linking actors n a network (e.g., exchange, kinship, communicative, affective, instrumental, or power relations)"</li>
<li>Density: The ratio of actual relations or ties among a set of actors in a network and the maximum possible number of ties.</li>
<li>Distance: A function of the number and strength of social ties separating two actors.</li>
<li>Dualism: The idea that the nature of groups is determined by the intersection of the actors within them (i.e., by the actions of their members), and that the nature of actors is determined by the intersection of groups "within" them i.e., by their group affiliations).</li>
<li>Egocentric network: An actor (sometimes called the "anchorage"), the actors with which it has relation, and the relations among those actors. This is sometimes referred to as a "personal network."</li>
<li>Form: The formal properties of the relations among actors in a network e.g., strength or weakness, density, symmetry or asymmetry).</li>
<li>Multiplex network: A network with two or more types of relations linking actors (e.g., exchange and communication in a market or communicative and affective ties n a clique).</li>
<li>Network: The set of social relations or social ties among a set of actors (and the actors themselves thus inked).</li>
<li>Network structure: The patterning of relations and "holes" among actors in a network. See also structural holes.</li>
<li>Position: A set of structurally equivalent actors or nodes (e.g., a block).</li>
<li>Positional approach: An analysis that focuses on the patterning of structurally equivalent relations among actors. See also relational approach.</li>
<li>Range: The number of an actor's ties to others. See also centrality.</li>
<li>Relational approach: An analysis that focuses on patterning of socially cohesive relations among actors. See also positional approach.</li>
<li>Role: The pattern of relations of a set of structurally equivalent actors (i.e., a block) to other blocks. Simultaneity, the principle of. The idea that all positions and roles (see above) are determined relative to one another and thus cannot be assumed or altered independently of one another.</li>
<li>Social circle: A group n which each actor s directly and strongly linked to most e.g., 80%), but not necessarily all, others. This is sometimes called a "social cluster." Compare clique.</li>
<li>Social cohesion: The presence of a dense network of strong ties among a set of actors. See also clique and social circle.</li>
<li>Social structure: The persisting pattern of ties among actors; more specifically, a network (microstructure) r the network of networks (macrostructure).</li>
<li>Strength of ties: The relative frequency, duration, emotional intensity, reciprocal exchange, and so on which characterize a given tie or set</li>
<li>Structural equivalence: The sharing, by a set of two or more actors who are not necessarily linked themselves, of equivalent relations to a</li>
<li>Structural hole: The absence of a relation among actors in a network (a crucial element of network structure).</li>
<li>Symmetric tie: A relation whose form and/or content is the same for the inked actors. See also asymmetric tie." (<a rel="noopener" href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/L5FUWHQM?page=38" target="_blank">Emirbayer and Goodwin 1994:1448-50</a>)</li>
</ul>
</div></div>
					</li>
				</ul>

			<li id="item_76BYYNDL" class="item journalArticle">
			<h2>Networked Justice: Judges, the Diffusion of Ideas, and Legal Reform Movements in Mexico</h2>
				<table>
					<tr>
						<th>Tipo</th>
						<td>Artículo de revista académica</td>
					</tr>
					<tr>
						<th class="author">Autor</th>
						<td>Matthew C. Ingram</td>
					</tr>
					<tr>
					<th>Resumen</th>
						<td>Existing research shows that the ideas of judges shape their behaviour. A natural next question to ask is, where do these ideas come from? Yet, there is little empirical evidence regarding the content and distribution of these ideas and even less evidence regarding the sources of these ideas, especially how ideas transfer or diffuse among judges. In this article, a survey of judges in the Mexican state of Michoacán generates original data on the attitudes and professional ties among these legal elites, and a mixed-methods design examines the diffusion of these attitudes along these ties, sequencing quantitative network analyses and interviews with judges to strengthen causal inferences. The core finding that the social structure of judges influences the attitudes judges hold contributes a valuable analytic complement to scholarship on comparative judicial behaviour, and clarifies our understanding of the role of judicial networks in strengthening democracy and the rule of law.
,
Estudios muestran que las ideas de los jueces moldean su comportamiento. Una segunda pregunta normal sería: ¿De dónde vienen esas ideas? Ahora bien, hay muy poca evidencia empírica en relación al contenido y distribución de tales ideas y todavía menos evidencia en relación a las fuentes de tales ideas, especialmente cómo las ideas se transfieren y difunden entre los jueces. En este artículo, una encuesta a jueces en el estado mexicano de Michoacán generaron datos sobre las actitudes y los lazos profesionales entre estas elites legales. Además, un diseño con varios métodos examina la difusión de estas actitudes a lo largo de tales lazos, enumerando análisis de redes cuantitativas y entrevistas con jueces para reforzar las inferencias causales. El hallazgo principal de que la estructura social de los jueces influye en las actitudes que ellos mismos mantienen contribuye a la academia con un complemento analítico valioso sobre el comportamiento judicial, y clarifica nuestro entendimiento sobre el papel de las redes judiciales en relación al fortalecimiento de la democracia y el estado de derecho.
,
Pesquisas existentes mostram como as ideias dos juízes moldam seus comportamentos. A pergunta natural que se segue é: de onde vêm estas ideias? No entanto, há pouca evidência empírica com relação ao conteúdo e distribuição destas ideias e, ainda menos, em relação à origem destas ideias, especialmente, como estas são transferidas ou difundem-se entre juízes. Neste artigo, um levantamento entre juízes do estado mexicano de Michoacán produziu dados originais acerca das atitudes e laços profissionais entre estas elites legais. A partir de métodos mistos de pesquisa examina-se a difusão dessas atitudes ao longo destas relações, intercala-se análises quantitativas de rede e entrevistas com juízes para reforçar inferências causais. A observação central de que a estrutura social na qual os juízes se inserem influencia suas atitudes representa uma valiosa contribuição analítica complementar para estudos sobre comportamento judicial comparativo, além de clarificar nossa compreensão acerca do papel das redes judiciais para o fortalecimento da democracia e do Estado de direito.</td>
					</tr>

				<h3 class="tags">Etiquetas:</h3>
				<ul class="tags">
					<li>listo y anotado</li>
					<li>ARS</li>
				</ul>
				<h3 class="notes">Notas:</h3>
				<ul class="notes">
					<li id="item_LBNXVM3I">
<div><p><strong>Extracted Annotations (16/12/2020 20:13:21)</strong></p>
<div>
<p>Estudios muestran que las ideas de los jueces moldean su comportamiento. Una segunda pregunta normal sería: ¿De dónde vienen esas ideas? Ahora bien, hay muy poca evidencia empírica en relación al contenido y distribución de tales ideas y todavía menos evidencia en relación a las fuentes de tales ideas, especialmente cómo las ideas se transfieren y difunden entre los jueces. En este artículo, una encuesta a jueces en el estado mexicano de Michoacán generaron datos sobre las actitudes y los lazos profesionales entre estas elites legales. Además, un diseño con varios métodos examina la difusión de estas actitudes a lo largo de tales lazos, enumerando análisis de redes cuantitativas y entrevistas con jueces para reforzar las inferencias causales. El hallazgo principal de que la estructura social de los jueces influye en las actitudes que ellos mismos mantienen contribuye a la academia con un complemento analítico valioso sobre el comportamiento judicial, y clarifica nuestro entendimiento sobre el papel de las redes judiciales en relación al fortalecimiento de la democracia y el estado de derecho.</p>
</div>
<div>
<h2>¿Por qué escogí este artículo?</h2>
</div>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Porque es un estudio en Michoacán.</li>
<li>Porque le interesa ver el aspecto político del derecho; el estudio de la situaciones políticas en el área purépecha --que es el tema que me interesa-- es tanto político como jurídico.</li>
<li>Porque utiliza metodología de redes sociales.</li>
<li>Artículos que conjuguen estos tres puntos son difíciles de encontrar, aún más por el aspecto de la metodología.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div>
<h2>Preguntas</h2>
</div>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Realismo jurídico. ¿De qué depende la aplicación de la justicia?</li>
<li>Actitudes de cambio y resistencia entre las élites jurídicas de Michoacán.</li>
<li>Contenido y distribución&nbsp;de las ideas entre los jueces y magistrados.</li>
<li>Transferencia y difusión&nbsp;de las ideas entre los aplicadores de justicia estatal.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div>
<h2>¿Cuál es la metodología que usa Ingram?</h2>
</div>
<div>
<blockquote>
<p>As noted by a recent review of network research,&nbsp;‘instead of worrying about national representativeness, progress may come from in-depth study in smaller settings’. This project is that kind of in-depth study in a smaller setting. (750)</p>
</blockquote>
</div>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Métodos mixtos. Diseño de investigación anidada (cuali y cuanti).</li>
<li>Aplicación de encuestas a personal jurídico estatal de Michoacán en 2011 contactados por teléfono y correo electrónico (90/110). Se identifican con códigos.</li>
<li>Análisis de redes: Enfoque que conjuga las interacciones individuales y las estructuras que surgen de esas interacciones.</li>
<li>Redes egocéntricas y redes sociocéntricas (personales y completa de la superposición de la egocéntricas; red de 113 actores depurada en 102).</li>
<li>Análisis&nbsp;formal&nbsp;de redes: medidas de grado, densidad, fuerza y centralidad.</li>
<li>Análisis&nbsp;cualitativo&nbsp;de redes en profundidad: cinco entrevistas semiestructuradas a actores relevantes de la red en Morelia para comprobar su validez externa e inferencia causal. Se les preguntó sobre sus impresiones sobre el análisis obtenido, si reflejaba sus idea de las relaciones entre lxs jueces y sobre el significado que ellxs atribuían a los vínculos.</li>
<li>Triangulación de los distintos datos cuali y cuanti.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div>
<h2>Conclusiones</h2>
</div>
<div>
<blockquote>
<p>In sum, quantitative analyses of network diffusion for ego- and socio-centric data complement each other in showing that two key factors influence ego’s attitude: (1) alters’ mean attitude, and (2) the strength of ties, that is, the intensity of interactions. Both of these key findings across different types of quantitative network analysis support the argument about the diffusion of ideas. (762)</p>
</blockquote>
</div>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Las ideas jurídicas no dependen de atributos indiviudales. Las ideas son interdependientes desde la perspectiva de la teoría de RS.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div>
<p>¿Te pareces con los que te juntas o te juntas con los que te pareces?&nbsp;Ingram concluye que las actitudes legales entre los jueces de Michoacán son definidos por la actitud media de sus contactos y la fuerza de dichas relaciones. Es más importante la fuerza y la frecuencia de las interacciones para actuar con ciertas actitudes en los juzgados.</p>
</div>
<div>
<blockquote>
<p>Further, regarding mechanisms of diffusion, interviews identified academic and professional mentorship relations as mechanisms underlying diffusion. Indeed, since most judges in Michoacán come from the state’s main public law school (following a pattern seen across the Mexican states), professors in these institutions who are concurrently or subsequently also judges may be particularly influential. This insight resonates with findings regarding the ‘infectiousness of ideas’ among law professors and clerks. (765)</p>
</blockquote>
</div>
<div>
<h2>Límites del estudio</h2>
</div>
<div>
<blockquote>
<p>¿Cuánta confianza debe situarse en la conclusión de que las interacciones judiciales configuran las actitudes judiciales, dado que los jueces con actitudes similares pueden ser llevados a interactuar más frecuentemente, en lugar de al revés? (750).</p>
</blockquote>
</div>
<div>
<p>Para eso también utiliza variables de control en las encuestas: edad, "progresividad" (continua de 1 a 7), orientación ideológica (1-10, después a tres dicotómicas), ingreso, posición profesional y distrito judicial. Se espera confirmar hipótesis sobre la correlación negativa entre edad y actitudes positivas a ciertas reformas, así como entre ingreso y actitud. Entre más edad, menos actitud favorable al cambio de reformas jurídicas.</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>Las actitudes de los actores que forman parte de la encuesta, pero que no fueron entrevistados se infieren de la información obtenida de las otras encuestas.</p>
</div>
<div>
<h2>¿Qué me falta?</h2>
</div>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Evidentemente estadística: probabilidad y regresiones lineales.</li>
<li>Como controlar por variables (homofilia, sexo, edad, ingreso).</li>
<li>Diseño de encuestas, creación y traducción de variables; unidades de observación medibles.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p>"In this article, a survey of judges in the Mexican state of Michoacán generates original data on the attitudes and professional ties among these legal elites, and a mixed-methods design examines the diffusion of these attitudes along these ties, sequencing quantitative network analyses and interviews with judges to strengthen causal inferences." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=1">Ingram 2016:739</a>)</p>
<p>"In the context of this debate on the role of judges in both institutional change and judicial decision-making, the ideas of judges play a prominent causal role in shaping key legal and judicial outcomes in Latin America." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=2">Ingram 2016:740</a>)</p>
<p>"judges play pivotal roles in either helping or hindering processes of legal changelegislative, institutional, and jurisprudentialdepending on their attitudes towards that change." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=3">Ingram 2016:741</a>)</p>
<p>"the ideas of judges matter for core legal outcomes that concern a wide range of political and socio-legal scholarship, in Latin America and beyond" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=3">Ingram 2016:741</a>)</p>
<p>"if ideas matter so much, where do they come from? How do ideas spread among judges?" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=3">Ingram 2016:741</a>)</p>
<p>"I conduct a network analysis of the diffusion of ideas among all judges in the Mexican state of Michoacán." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=3">Ingram 2016:741</a>)</p>
<p>"diffusion is very difficult to study." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=3">Ingram 2016:741</a>)</p>
<p>"The tools of network analysis lend themselves to this endeavour, yet causal inference about diffusion remains challenging even in network analysis, especially in contexts with limited relational data and no temporal variation in data." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=3">Ingram 2016:741</a>)</p>
<p>"Specifically, I follow recent advice that network research should adopt more" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=3">Ingram 2016:741</a>)</p>
<p>"local levels of analysis in order to increase analytic leverage in the study of network effects, and I sequence quantitative network analysis with qualitative, in-depth interviews." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=4">Ingram 2016:742</a>)</p>
<p>"the qualitative phase of this project helps clarify how judges themselves understand the origins of their own ideas, that is, how they attribute meaning to their ties and relations with other judges, complementing the quantitative analysis to help identify the causal effects of judicial networks." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=4">Ingram 2016:742</a>)</p>
<p>"Complementing literatures on comparative judicial politics, sub-national politics, policy diffusion, and network analysis, a relationship between the social structure among judges and their attitudes is found. I call this phenomenon'networked justice'." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=4">Ingram 2016:742</a>)</p>
<p>"This local, mixed-methods, embedded design offers analytic purchase that is otherwise absent in designs that might pursue similar questions at more aggregate levels of analysis or by using either method in isolation." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=4">Ingram 2016:742</a>)</p>
<p>"In greater detail, the project makes four main contributions: () original data on the variation in attitudes of judges regarding prominent institutional and jurisprudential changes shaping the legal landscape in Mexico; () personal, egocentric network data for individual judges; () group, socio-centric data for the judicial network in the whole state generated by aggregating the egocentric data; and () an analysis of the causal relationship between network structure and judicial attitudes." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=4">Ingram 2016:742</a>)</p>
<p>"The following section introduces the reader to the landscape of legal change in Mexico, emphasising the extent to which patterns seen in Mexico are illustrative of patterns seen elsewhere in the region and in other parts of the world." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=5">Ingram 2016:743</a>)</p>
<p>"the fifth section the data are presented and the sequence of methods introduced." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=5">Ingram 2016:743</a>)</p>
<p>"Notably, the egocentric, socio-centric and qualitative portions of the analysis require different methods, and the approach to each of these phases is outlined separately in this section." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=5">Ingram 2016:743</a>)</p>
<p>"The empirical analysis is concentrated in the sixth and seventh sections: thefirst part of the sixth section examines the egocentric data, and the second part analyses the socio-centric data generated by aggregating the egocentric data; the seventh section offers qualitative evidence from personal interviews with focal individuals." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=5">Ingram 2016:743</a>)</p>
<p>"I find consistent and robust evidence that social structure influences judicial attitudes." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=5">Ingram 2016:743</a>)</p>
<p>"network analysis is a promising tool to examine ideas and how these transfer among relevant actors." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=5">Ingram 2016:743</a>)</p>
<p>"In decision-making (judicial behaviour on the bench) attitudes, values and ideology play a critical role in determining the willingness of judges to review" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=5">Ingram 2016:743</a>)</p>
<p>"particular cases, to address certain issues and in determining thefinal outcome of cases." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=6">Ingram 2016:744</a>)</p>
<p>"In addition to shaping judicial decision-making, ideational factors also motivate and shape the behaviour of judges off the bench, activities of judges for and against institutional reforms." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=6">Ingram 2016:744</a>)</p>
<p>"In sum, institutional" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=6">Ingram 2016:744</a>)</p>
<p>"insiders (judges) and their subjective, non-material commitments play an important role in explaining crucial judicial outcomes." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=7">Ingram 2016:745</a>)</p>
<p>"while we know the ideas of judges matter, there is little empirical evidence regarding the content and distribution of these ideas and even less evidence regarding how these ideas transfer or diffuse among judges." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=7">Ingram 2016:745</a>)</p>
<p>"we know very little about the content and distribution of judicial attitudes" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=7">Ingram 2016:745</a>)</p>
<p>"Further, these metrics do not ask judges themselves about their attitudes. Here, I conceptualise ideas specifically as attitudes towards existing legal reforms (e.g., the creation of judicial councils) and styles of decision-making (e.g., whether lower-court judges should always have to defer to the decisions of higher courts). The survey questionnaire captures a wide range of attitudes regarding these institutional and jurisprudential topics and relies on judges' self-reports to identify their attitudes." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=8">Ingram 2016:746</a>)</p>
<p>"we know even less about how these attitudes transfer or diffuse among judges." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=8">Ingram 2016:746</a>)</p>
<p>"Ideational profiles are understood as the product of an individual's features, for example, socioeconomic status." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=8">Ingram 2016:746</a>)</p>
<p>"social relations and interactions with other individuals may account for a larger part of the origin of a judge's ideational profile." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=8">Ingram 2016:746</a>)</p>
<p>"To be clear, attention to relational sources of legal change and law reform networks is not new." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=8">Ingram 2016:746</a>)</p>
<p>"Woods explains the emergence of'consensus around norms' as the result of sustained interaction within relatively diffuse'judicial communities', groups of judges who also share similar demographic characteristics such as education and professional trajectory. However, the treatment of network concepts is informal in the research cited above. Even where the notion of networks and diffusion effects are referenced more explicitly, network concepts remain largely informal." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=8">Ingram 2016:746</a>)</p>
<p>"structural, network-analytic terms," (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=8">Ingram 2016:746</a>)</p>
<p>"harnessing a fuller set of conceptual, measurement and analytic techniques for the study of judicial networks." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=9">Ingram 2016:747</a>)</p>
<p>"Network analysis also has some methodological advantages for examining the diffusion of ideas." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=9">Ingram 2016:747</a>)</p>
<p>"the adoption of a new idea is fundamentally understood as an individualistic or atomistic phenomenon, based on the properties, features or attributes of isolated individuals. Conversely, a network perspective conceptualises units of analysis as interdependent; judicial attitudes may be shaped in part by individual attributes, but they are also a function of the attitudes of other judges." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=9">Ingram 2016:747</a>)</p>
<p>"Mexico offers a promising environment in which to study justice reform networks." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=10">Ingram 2016:748</a>)</p>
<p>", existing research offers qualitative evidence of judges who act as reform entrepreneurs or agents of socialisation, constituting the kind of justice reform networks the present study seeks to formalise in a more systematic manner." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=10">Ingram 2016:748</a>)</p>
<p>"For instance, a group of judges from the state of Michoacán formed a close-knit" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=10">Ingram 2016:748</a>)</p>
<p>"group that promoted the judicial council reform in that state from 2002 onwards, and members of this group have since also promoted the criminal procedure reform." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=11">Ingram 2016:749</a>)</p>
<p>"Several members of this group, led by state supreme court judge Alejandro González Gómez and state electoral judge Jaime del Río, studied law together in Spain at the Universidad Complutense de Madrid and were influenced by the teachings and experiences of progressive judges who lived through Spain's transition from Franco's dictatorship to democracy in the lates ands, including the'Democratic Justice' movement." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=11">Ingram 2016:749</a>)</p>
<p>"these individuals' academic and professional presence influenced colleagues and newer generations of legal professionals." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=11">Ingram 2016:749</a>)</p>
<p>"given the breadth and depth of legal reforms being pursued in Mexico, the country offers a rich environment in which to study the diffusion of ideas among judges that might help or hinder such a process. However, as in many larger federal systems, the implementation of many reforms in Mexico, including the judicial council and criminal procedure reforms, are left to the states. Many states have not promoted these reforms, while others have advanced far." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=11">Ingram 2016:749</a>)</p>
<p>"a good state in which to conduct this research is one in which there is some evidence of variation in the attitudes of judges towards these reforms. Again, Michoacán provides this variation to a much greater degree than other states." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=11">Ingram 2016:749</a>)</p>
<p>"'instead of worrying about national representativeness, progress may come from in-depth study in smaller settings'." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=12">Ingram 2016:750</a>)</p>
<p>"judges who are more connected will tend to share similar attitudes, capturing the diffusion argument." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=12">Ingram 2016:750</a>)</p>
<p>"This study applies quantitative and qualitative methods to the analysis of the relationship between judicial networks and judicial attitudes." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=12">Ingram 2016:750</a>)</p>
<p>"regarding the potential endogenous relationship between network structure and attitudes." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=12">Ingram 2016:750</a>)</p>
<p>"That is, how much confidence should be placed in the conclusion that judicial interactions shape judicial attitudes given that judges with similar attitudes may be drawn to interact more frequently, rather than the other way around?" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=12">Ingram 2016:750</a>)</p>
<p>"Sokhey and Djupe,'Interpersonal Networks', p.; see also Richard Snyder,'Scaling Down: The Subnational Comparative Method', Studies in Comparative International Development, : (), pp.-." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=12">Ingram 2016:750</a>)</p>
<p>", I rely on the alternative, a mixed-methods approach sequencing quantitative and qualitative network analysis, toflesh out the causal relationship between network structure and attitudes." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=13">Ingram 2016:751</a>)</p>
<p>"a mixed-methods strategy is employed in two ways: (1) in the combination of ego (egocentric) and whole (socio-centric) network data and analysis; and (2) in the combination of quantitative and qualitative methods." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=13">Ingram 2016:751</a>)</p>
<p>"Notably, in addition to nesting qualitative evidence within the sample of observations analysed quantitatively to form an'embedded' network design, I also rely on two different forms of quantitative network analysis: egoand socio-centric" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=13">Ingram 2016:751</a>)</p>
<p>"Since each ego network is sampled independently of the others, these data can be studied with standard regression techniques that treat each observation as independent." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=13">Ingram 2016:751</a>)</p>
<p>"Second, the egocentric data is aggregated to form sociocentric networks, thereby drawing on the strengths of each type of data to offset their weaknesses. Network regressions that account for the structural dependence among observations model these socio-centric data." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=13">Ingram 2016:751</a>)</p>
<p>"the research design combines these two forms of quantitative network analysis (personal and whole) with in-depth, qualitative network analysis." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=13">Ingram 2016:751</a>)</p>
<p>"using quantitative tools to selectfive judges for personal, semi-structured interviews in order to gain a'better understanding of how networks matter and of what mechanisms and conditionsfigure in when producing certain network outcomes'" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=14">Ingram 2016:752</a>)</p>
<p>"he triangulation of data and methods of analysis inherent in this combination enhances the quality of the measures and the validity offinal conclusions regarding causation." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=14">Ingram 2016:752</a>)</p>
<p>"Of this total, telephonic contacts sought a full census of these judges but obtained 85 responses. A follow-up effort via email obtained an additionalfive responses, yielding a total of 90 completed questionnaires, for a response rate of 81.92 per cent. Once the initial data analysis was complete, personal interviews withfive focal individuals were conducted in the state capital, Morelia, in January 2012." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=14">Ingram 2016:752</a>)</p>
<p>"Density is the number of ties as a proportion of the total possible ties." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=14">Ingram 2016:752</a>)</p>
<p>"Tie strength was measured by asking respondents how close they were to each alter and how close each of the alters were to each other (cercanía)." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=14">Ingram 2016:752</a>)</p>
<p>"Following Betsy Sinclair's advice, additional variables must control for homophily and confounders that might be ascribed to context. Homophily is the similarity between nodes on individual attributes that might cause these individuals to have the attitude of interest. Thus, control variables include age, progressiveness, ideological orientation, highest level of education, income, professional" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=14">Ingram 2016:752</a>)</p>
<p>"position and judicial district." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=15">Ingram 2016:753</a>)</p>
<p>"Progressiveness is captured by an ordinal variable generated by judges placing themselves on a continuum from traditional to progressive (-). A second question asks judges to place themselves on a left-right scale of ideological orientation (-; = left, = right). This variable was transformed to create three dichotomous variables (- = left,- = centre,- = right)." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=15">Ingram 2016:753</a>)</p>
<p>"Table summarises descriptive statistics for ego's attitude on four legal issues, network composition on these issues (alters' mean attitude), ego's demographic characteristics, and structural features of personal network." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=15">Ingram 2016:753</a>)</p>
<p>"Next, the egocentric data is aggregated to generate socio-centric network data." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=15">Ingram 2016:753</a>)</p>
<p>"dummy variable" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=15">Ingram 2016:753</a>)</p>
<p>"Ingram, Rodríguez-Ferreira, and Shirk found that age negatively correlated with positive attitudes towards certain reforms." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=15">Ingram 2016:753</a>)</p>
<p>" if second-instance magistrado, if first-instance juez" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=15">Ingram 2016:753</a>)</p>
<p>"thus, we can get a fuller sense of the structure of social relations between these judges byfinding the ways in which their social structure overlaps, weaving personal networks together into one large, whole network." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=15">Ingram 2016:753</a>)</p>
<p>"for all practical purposes, the data capture a full network of all judges in the state." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=15">Ingram 2016:753</a>)</p>
<p>"The attitudes of judges who did not participate in the survey (i.e., alters who were named by survey participants but who did not themselves participate in survey) were established by averaging the responses provided by participants." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=15">Ingram 2016:753</a>)</p>
<p>"the full, connected network consists of nodes with varying demographic and attitudinal characteristics and edges of varying strength. The nodes constitute. per cent of the names on the official directory of judges. Figure visualises the full network. Node size is based on number of ties (degree centrality); edge colour reflects tie strength (strongest in black); and node colour reflects attitude towards judicial councils (low to high passing from blue, through yellow, to red). Table summarises statistics for this socio-centric network." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=16">Ingram 2016:754</a>)</p>
<p>"First, the prominent group of judges on the state supreme court is, for the most part, centrally located." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=16">Ingram 2016:754</a>)</p>
<p>"Second, while judges are assigned to judicial districts that correspond" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=17">Ingram 2016:755</a>)</p>
<p>"with geographic areas across the state, several judges assigned to areas outside the state capital are nonetheless centrally located in the network, alongside state supreme court judges from the capital." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=18">Ingram 2016:756</a>)</p>
<p>"Some observers may wonder about the clustered nature of the dependent variable. That is, is it a problem that so many of the units seem to have similar values?" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=18">Ingram 2016:756</a>)</p>
<p>"Indeed, it is this convergence around a value or set of values that is of interest here, since it suggests that relational networks may help explain why judges hold similar attitudes. As noted more than years ago by Galton (), clustering is itself a sign of interdependence." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=18">Ingram 2016:756</a>)</p>
<p>"In the socio-centric analysis of the network represented in Figure, the key explanatory variable is the mean value of the attitude of each of a node's neighbours (neighbourhood mean). Additional explanatory variables operationalise centrality in the overall network, homophily (similarity between any two judges) and contextual factors." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=18">Ingram 2016:756</a>)</p>
<p>"Egocentric networks" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=18">Ingram 2016:756</a>)</p>
<p>"Results" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=18">Ingram 2016:756</a>)</p>
<p>"Given the ordinal dependent variable (ego's attitude), ordered probabilistic regressions were applied to the egocentric data. The main explanatory variable is the mean value of the attitude among the ego's alters, capturing the attitudinal composition of the network." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=18">Ingram 2016:756</a>)</p>
<p>"The key predictor alters' mean(y), has the expected positive relationship with ego's attitude, and this result is statistically significant. Similarly, mean tie strength has a positive and statistically significant relationship." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=19">Ingram 2016:757</a>)</p>
<p>"The probability of the lowest attitude (y =) is highest where alters' mean attitude is at its lowest; in this instance, there is about an per cent likelihood that ego's attitude has the lowest value if alters' mean is at its lowest value" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=19">Ingram 2016:757</a>)</p>
<p>"Conversely, there is approximately a per cent likelihood of the highest outcome (y =) if mean(y) is also at its highest value." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=19">Ingram 2016:757</a>)</p>
<p>"In short, a judge's attitude towards judicial councils is shaped by his or her colleagues' attitudes towards councils. Taken in" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=19">Ingram 2016:757</a>)</p>
<p>"combination with thefinding regarding tie strength, this is systematic, empirical support for the proposition that intense interaction promotes ideational diffusion." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=20">Ingram 2016:758</a>)</p>
<p>"In each analysis, mean attitude among alters maintains its positive and statistically significant relationship with ego's attitude on the same issue." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=21">Ingram 2016:759</a>)</p>
<p>"The key variable of interest (the mean attitude of all contacts one step away from each judge) has a positive coefficient across all models, providing general support for the proposition that a judge's attitude towards council reform increases as the attitude towards said reform increases among a judge's close colleagues." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=21">Ingram 2016:759</a>)</p>
<p>"the mere presence of a direct relation between ego and alter is not sufficient to influence ego's attitude; rather, the influence of direct relations is contingent on the strength or intensity of that relation. Thus, the socio-centric analysis generates strong support for H. The findings clearly complement thefindings from the egocentric analysis, where both alters' mean attitude and tie strength had positive, statistically significant relationships with the ego's attitude towards judicial councils." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=22">Ingram 2016:760</a>)</p>
<p>"Two patterns should be highlighted from these graphs. First, the slope of the probability curves in the graphs supports the expected relationships. Specifically, in thefirst graph, it is more likely that ego will hold the most negative attitude towards judicial councils if her peers hold a negative attitude." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=23">Ingram 2016:761</a>)</p>
<p>"Conversely, in the last graph, it is dramatically more likely that a judge will hold the most positive attitude towards judicial councils if her peers hold a" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=23">Ingram 2016:761</a>)</p>
<p>"positive attitude than if they hold the most negative attitude." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=24">Ingram 2016:762</a>)</p>
<p>"Second, however, the relationship is only clearly significant for the highest value of the outcome variable. Thus, the evidence is still complementary of the egocentric analysis, but only for the highest value of the outcome variable." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=24">Ingram 2016:762</a>)</p>
<p>"In sum, quantitative analyses of network diffusion for egoand socio-centric data complement each other in showing that two key factors influence ego's attitude: () alters' mean attitude, and () the strength of ties, that is, the intensity of interactions. Both of these keyfindings across different types of quantitative network analysis support the argument about the diffusion of ideas." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=24">Ingram 2016:762</a>)</p>
<p>"The substantive part of the analysis addresses two issues () external validity of network structure, and () validity of causal inferences) and draws on a set offive personal, in-depth interviews with judges who participated in the survey generating the network data above." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=24">Ingram 2016:762</a>)</p>
<p>"All of the interview participants are in the top half of typicality scores, and two of them are in the top per cent. Thus, these are promising observations in which we might expect tofind additional evidence of the central argument tested in the quantitative analysis." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=25">Ingram 2016:763</a>)</p>
<p>"They were then asked to focus on two questions: () whether the network structure reflected their own mental image of social relations among judges (external validity), and () what meaning they themselves attributed to those ties and the network structure now visualised (causal inference)." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=25">Ingram 2016:763</a>)</p>
<p>"Regarding external validity,,,, and, (all magistrados) immediately recognised the visualisation of the network of the state supreme court as a fair representation of a split between primarily two groups of judges, including a core group of more progressive judges spearheading changes in institutional design and jurisprudence. Each of these judges also spontaneously volunteered his or her guesses about which magistrados were part of the core group and which were more peripheral; a clear majority of these unsolicited observations were correct. Thus, the transition from questionnaire to network visualisation appears to faithfully reproduce social structures that members of the court recognise from their own daily experience." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=25">Ingram 2016:763</a>)</p>
<p>", noted that she feels influenced by those individuals with whom she is in contact. Asked specifically whether the people with whom she interacts most frequently, her judicial discussion group, shaped her attitudes and ideas, she affirmed that this was the case." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=26">Ingram 2016:764</a>)</p>
<p>"Over sustained interactions, she said, this group has come to have similar ideas." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=26">Ingram 2016:764</a>)</p>
<p>"they held similar ideas because of the frequency of interactions" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=26">Ingram 2016:764</a>)</p>
<p>"In sum, the interview evidence supports the network influencefinding, adding context and depth regarding certain structural features of the network. Further, regarding mechanisms of diffusion, interviews identified academic and professional mentorship relations as mechanisms underlying diffusion. Indeed, since most judges in Michoacán come from the state's main public law school (following a pattern seen across the Mexican states), professors in these institutions who are concurrently or subsequently also judges may be particularly influential. This insight resonates withfindings regarding the'infectiousness of ideas' among law professors and clerks." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=27">Ingram 2016:765</a>)</p>
<p>"the analysis has deep theoretical and policy implications for scholarly understanding of legal reform and the behaviour of legal professionals in Latin America." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=27">Ingram 2016:765</a>)</p>
<p>"In the context of this debate on the role of judges in both institutional change and judicial decision-making, the ideas of judges play a prominent causal role in shaping key legal and judicial outcomes in Latin America." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=27">Ingram 2016:765</a>)</p>
<p>"thefindings strongly support the proposition that attitudes and other ideas about legal reform diffuse in systematic and identifiable ways among judges." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=28">Ingram 2016:766</a>)</p>
<p>"these findings support thinking of judges as interconnected or interrelated with each other in ways that affect how they think about the law and legal institutions. This attitudinal interdependence challenges much of the existing literature that focuses exclusively on factors specific to isolated individuals, rather than treating judges as interconnected with other judges and legal institutions as interconnected with other legal institutions." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=28">Ingram 2016:766</a>)</p>
<p>"we need to theorise how multiple types of interrelated connections exert an influence across judges, other legal professionals and the institutions that house them, perhaps drawing on interdisciplinary literatures on complex systems" (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=28">Ingram 2016:766</a>)</p>
<p>". The conceptual, theoretical and methodological tools of network analysis, including the theoretical insights above, offer concrete ways for mapping and analysing that social architecture in order to maximise the chances of success for myriad reform projects." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=29">Ingram 2016:767</a>)</p>
<p>"In sum, the project contributes original network data for judges in a large state in Mexico, and pairs these data with interview evidence in a mixedmethods network design to show how key attitudes diffuse among judges in empirically identifiable ways." (<a href="zotero://open-pdf/library/items/7I9F8JEG?page=29">Ingram 2016:767</a>)</p></div>
					</li>
					<li id="item_IUIKN2ZQ">
<div><p>Nota 1</p>
<div>
<p>Estudios muestran que las ideas de los jueces moldean su comportamiento. Una segunda pregunta normal sería: ¿De dónde vienen esas ideas? Ahora bien, hay muy poca evidencia empírica en relación al contenido y distribución de tales ideas y todavía menos evidencia en relación a las fuentes de tales ideas, especialmente cómo las ideas se transfieren y difunden entre los jueces. En este artículo, una encuesta a jueces en el estado mexicano de Michoacán generaron datos sobre las actitudes y los lazos profesionales entre estas elites legales. Además, un diseño con varios métodos examina la difusión de estas actitudes a lo largo de tales lazos, enumerando análisis de redes cuantitativas y entrevistas con jueces para reforzar las inferencias causales. El hallazgo principal de que la estructura social de los jueces influye en las actitudes que ellos mismos mantienen contribuye a la academia con un complemento analítico valioso sobre el comportamiento judicial, y clarifica nuestro entendimiento sobre el papel de las redes judiciales en relación al fortalecimiento de la democracia y el estado de derecho.</p>
</div>
<div>
<h2>¿Por qué escogí este artículo?</h2>
</div>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Porque es un estudio en Michoacán.</li>
<li>Porque le interesa ver el aspecto político del derecho; el estudio de la situaciones políticas en el área purépecha --que es el tema que me interesa-- es tanto político como jurídico.</li>
<li>Porque utiliza metodología de redes sociales.</li>
<li>Artículos que conjuguen estos tres puntos son difíciles de encontrar, aún más por el aspecto de la metodología.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div>
<h2>Preguntas</h2>
</div>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Realismo jurídico. ¿De qué depende la aplicación de la justicia?</li>
<li>Actitudes de cambio y resistencia entre las élites jurídicas de Michoacán.</li>
<li>Contenido y distribución&nbsp;de las ideas entre los jueces y magistrados.</li>
<li>Transferencia y difusión&nbsp;de las ideas entre los aplicadores de justicia estatal.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div>
<h2>¿Cuál es la metodología que usa Ingram?</h2>
</div>
<div>
<blockquote>
<p>As noted by a recent review of network research,&nbsp;‘instead of worrying about national representativeness, progress may come from in-depth study in smaller settings’. This project is that kind of in-depth study in a smaller setting. (750)</p>
</blockquote>
</div>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Métodos mixtos. Diseño de investigación anidada (cuali y cuanti).</li>
<li>Aplicación de encuestas a personal jurídico estatal de Michoacán en 2011 contactados por teléfono y correo electrónico (90/110). Se identifican con códigos.</li>
<li>Análisis de redes: Enfoque que conjuga las interacciones individuales y las estructuras que surgen de esas interacciones.</li>
<li>Redes egocéntricas y redes sociocéntricas (personales y completa de la superposición de la egocéntricas; red de 113 actores depurada en 102).</li>
<li>Análisis&nbsp;formal&nbsp;de redes: medidas de grado, densidad, fuerza y centralidad.</li>
<li>Análisis&nbsp;cualitativo&nbsp;de redes en profundidad: cinco entrevistas semiestructuradas a actores relevantes de la red en Morelia para comprobar su validez externa e inferencia causal. Se les preguntó sobre sus impresiones sobre el análisis obtenido, si reflejaba sus idea de las relaciones entre lxs jueces y sobre el significado que ellxs atribuían a los vínculos.</li>
<li>Triangulación de los distintos datos cuali y cuanti.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div>
<h2>Conclusiones</h2>
</div>
<div>
<blockquote>
<p>In sum, quantitative analyses of network diffusion for ego- and socio-centric data complement each other in showing that two key factors influence ego’s attitude: (1) alters’ mean attitude, and (2) the strength of ties, that is, the intensity of interactions. Both of these key findings across different types of quantitative network analysis support the argument about the diffusion of ideas. (762)</p>
</blockquote>
</div>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Las ideas jurídicas no dependen de atributos indiviudales. Las ideas son interdependientes desde la perspectiva de la teoría de RS.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div>
<p>¿Te pareces con los que te juntas o te juntas con los que te pareces?&nbsp;Ingram concluye que las actitudes legales entre los jueces de Michoacán son definidos por la actitud media de sus contactos y la fuerza de dichas relaciones. Es más importante la fuerza y la frecuencia de las interacciones para actuar con ciertas actitudes en los juzgados.</p>
</div>
<div>
<blockquote>
<p>Further, regarding mechanisms of diffusion, interviews identified academic and professional mentorship relations as mechanisms underlying diffusion. Indeed, since most judges in Michoacán come from the state’s main public law school (following a pattern seen across the Mexican states), professors in these institutions who are concurrently or subsequently also judges may be particularly influential. This insight resonates with findings regarding the ‘infectiousness of ideas’ among law professors and clerks. (765)</p>
</blockquote>
</div>
<div>
<h2>Límites del estudio</h2>
</div>
<div>
<blockquote>
<p>¿Cuánta confianza debe situarse en la conclusión de que las interacciones judiciales configuran las actitudes judiciales, dado que los jueces con actitudes similares pueden ser llevados a interactuar más frecuentemente, en lugar de al revés? (750).</p>
</blockquote>
</div>
<div>
<p>Para eso también utiliza variables de control en las encuestas: edad, "progresividad" (continua de 1 a 7), orientación ideológica (1-10, después a tres dicotómicas), ingreso, posición profesional y distrito judicial. Se espera confirmar hipótesis sobre la correlación negativa entre edad y actitudes positivas a ciertas reformas, así como entre ingreso y actitud. Entre más edad, menos actitud favorable al cambio de reformas jurídicas.</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>Las actitudes de los actores que forman parte de la encuesta, pero que no fueron entrevistados se infieren de la información obtenida de las otras encuestas.</p>
</div>
<div>
<h2>¿Qué me falta?</h2>
</div>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Evidentemente estadística: probabilidad y regresiones lineales.</li>
<li>Como controlar por variables (homofilia, sexo, edad, ingreso).</li>
<li>Diseño de encuestas, creación y traducción de variables; unidades de observación medibles.</li>
</ul>
</div></div>
					</li>
				</ul>
